[2023-10-02 17:51:24] 204320873719660544: @shlomohayat234 , @YT Master Gaming 

David said:
> Regarding tracks that you've already made, there isn't a function at this time that allows you to go back and modify it (yet) 

you can go back to one of the continuations, and start a *new* Continue branch... or regenerate that chirp  to start a *new* branch there...

Either way add [Instrumental] and nothing else to the chirp text field where your lyrics go  (or your new lyrics).

you won't get the exact same clip with your edits..., you will get a new Continuation with your edits.

(apologize if that is obvious, but I have gone back and started a new branch and taken it from there....)

[2023-10-04 10:20:55] 614946962139250711: piano and strings yeah, though instruments are more hit or than genres. And I've found the more specific you get the less likely to work. It's always good to search the discord public channels to see what other terms people used, especially when trying for things that are trickier to prompt like non vocal music. (And you can even continue from an sample that already exists if it happened to be a perfect fit for what you were aiming for!)
[2023-10-04 10:36:58] 169591641684967425: if specificity is what messes things up could that just be a result of data being labeled too broadly?

[2023-10-04 10:39:20] 614946962139250711: I'm purely speculating and have no idea really, but I'd guess that labeling a song with 'bagpipes' for example is both less common because of less songs overall, and just a lower priority for whatever analysis is doing the labeling, versus 'piano' or something extremely common. So if you want bagpipes, works better to prompt with genres that use that instrument in my experience.

[2023-10-04 14:56:43] 614946962139250711: I often prefix creative ChatGPT requests something like this (just an random example didn't try this on lyrics where I think you'd want to be more explicit) `First, think of two pairs of random letters from the alphabet. For each pair of random letters, pick 5 lesser known fiction author and song writer with those initials. Then using the fourth randomly selected pair of writers you picked and distinct writing style and language use as inspiration, write whatever` 

works better if you pick the random letters yourself, works better still if you break it into two requests so ChatGPT picks the writers in a first, seperate, request that doesn't contain the part about what to write after. Though it still helps diversity somewhat if you just literally prompt that, it just tends to pick the same 'random' initials and people over and over... like Kafka comes up ALL THE TIME somehow lol. And you can always do the classic followup make-it-better prompt, like maybe "Okay now writing as a new author who thinks those lyrics have *terrible* flow (or whatever) write a vastly improved version that is better.."

[2023-10-04 22:54:37] 407677463548919828: Seriously though.

You chirp = it makes music.

You chirp, then pick which one you want to continue, then keep doing that again until you feel the song is over.  Then you heart the last option you would have normally continued and that will stitch the whole thing into one song.

[2023-10-05 16:38:41] 407677463548919828: Otherwise suggestions I've seen include trying to make sure you stay consistent within a thirty second window, avoiding anything that ends on a radical change between segments (it gets harder to get back) so say you want an instrumental, try including it before the verses of a segment not at the end.  Another suggestion I've seen is to have a sort of coda or refrain that gets repeated often to keep the results consistent.  Your resul*t*s may vary at this of course.

[2023-10-06 02:05:53] 1159661481323942020: how do you get a full song
[2023-10-06 02:39:10] 850192027022131210: /chipr
[2023-10-06 02:41:52] 1024867715917303861: Hey gate 👋 well to answer your question I'd need to break it down into three parts...

a) #🐣┃how-to-chirp will better explain how to use the bot

b) #⏩┃continuation will explain how to extend generation to the length of the song you want to create

c) lastly, song structure. This in of itself is a very unique-to-user design. Some prefer to start with an intro, some prefer to begin with a verse. The ChatGPT that is housed within the bot will construct a verse to chorus structure. If you'd like to define it differently it would be better for you to use your own lyrics in the lyrical section above it. To properly organize your song include the song segment (whether it be a intro, verse, chorus, bridge, fade out outro) in brackets, at the beginning of your lyrical section prior to the lyrics. 
For example...

 [intro}

*This is where the lyrics go
If I want to make a flow
or build something that I can show 
To the people that I know*

Again the structure of your song can be as unique as you want it to be. There is no perfect way about it, play around and have fun and do whatever sounds good to you.

When you finish, you can show off your work in #🐣┃suno-showcase 

Hopes this helps.

[2023-10-10 23:56:37] 614946962139250711: One thing that could be made clear is some tags are pretty reliable like [chorus] and [verse]. And as I understand it (guessing from what Suno devs say in chat) those tags are more deliberately put into Chirp. 

But many other tags are just things the AI learned, and it's not just a list that even Suno knows 100% - so the best tags really have to be discovered and tested, the same way people find good Stable Diffusion prompts. Prompting for chords is probably not going to work. However I tested Chords and it *might * have been working a *little* bit (more than random chance) but I'm not sure. Overall I would consider chords not working for now. But I am quite curious if the AI actually can be prompted with Chords more effectively even thoug it really shouldn't work...
[2023-10-11 00:05:14] 614946962139250711: Heads up that Chirp V1 didn't have a music style field, so if you go back too far the advice is not directly relevant. Though the concepts may still be useful, for example, you might prompt the first segment of your song focusing 100% on music style, using tags and fake lyrics as part of that to try and get just the right music, and then starting your real song as a continue from that segment. [2023-10-12 13:08:32] 456226577798135808: yo
[2023-10-12 13:09:12] 614946962139250711: If you don't separate by , it is treated like one word. you can also repeat, `guitar, guitar, male, male` and it can sometimes make the effect stronger.
[2023-10-12 13:11:08] 204320873719660544: > And is the “,” can make a difference?

It's an LLM (like chatgpt, but nowhere near as big) so it will *interpret* what you type.... sometimes it will accept my typos, sometimes it gives up trying to figure out what "smoky voice chanteuse" means and does nothing....

Don't get toooo granular in your thinking... that sort of subtlety is probably *less* than the AI's built-in randomness....

But of course you should try what you think might work, and maybe expect nothing is ever 100%...

[2023-10-14 14:12:36] 381493791250710538: How do i get more seconds for the music ?
[2023-10-14 14:13:09] 381493791250710538: or is this mpossible?
[2023-10-14 14:21:12] 407677463548919828: You hit the continue button on the segment you liked best. If you didn't like either one, then you try again until you do then continue that.
[2023-10-14 14:22:03] 407677463548919828: Once you have reached the end of your song (or if you just need to be sure that all the pieces fit together correctly) hit the heart on the last part you liked and it will go back up the chain and stitch together all the segements to make one full song for you.

Good luck!

[2023-10-15 00:11:33] 407677463548919828: `/chirp` 

**Describe the type of music:**  `industrial, synthpop, instrumental, instrumental, instrumental, instrumental, instrumental, synthwave`

**Enter your own lyrics:**

`[Intro]

[upbeat music]
[harsh drumbeat]

Ha-ha-ha-ha-ha

[train whistle]
[instrumental]`


And like I said, I'd leave the ChatGPT field empty.

I have no idea if this would work or not, but it's what I'd try for my first roll.

Why the "Ha-ha-ha-ha-ha" in there?  Because sometimes stuff like that can guide the AI. Sometimes it does nothing, and sometimes you wasted your time.
[2023-10-15 00:12:57] 407677463548919828: One thing I definitely encourage you to do is write *everything* you try in the song in a notepad or something, and **save** that text.  It will make it easier for you to figure out what to add or remove.
[2023-10-15 00:13:23] 407677463548919828: Another thing is not to overwhelm it with a bunch of stuff all at once.  The AI becomes aware of time pressure then.
[2023-10-15 00:14:13] 407677463548919828: One thing to look out for is the AI *wants* to use vocals.  So it will usually give you the first one because it says [Intro] in it.  After than generations may be shorter than usual because it's waiting for you to put in the lyrics.

[2023-10-16 15:14:01] 211004396765577216: the continuations get more robotic. The first generation is typically good
[2023-10-16 15:22:52] 407677463548919828: I don't know if there is a *real* solution for this.  What I do is ocasionally I can go back up a few segments and recreate them without the issue and continue from there as per normal even if it means giving up a specific bit I liked in the original.

Occasionally what also works is editing.  That requires you give up on any complete version from Chirp though.

For this to work, you must have already written the lyrics you plan to use and have a chorus ready.

Save the first segment by hearting what you have up to where things started going wrong for you.

Then you go back to the times where the segment sounded "correct" to you and continue from there with new entirely different lyrics, replacing the original with the second verse or third verse depending on where you are.  You continue on from there and heart it when you're happy with that progress, saving that chain.

You do this until you have all the chains you need, including a good [outro] or [fade out] and throw the parts into the audio editor of your choice and attempt to edit the pieces together to make a new whole song.

This can be a lot of work but when done right it can give you the consistent sound and quality you were looking for.
[2023-10-16 15:23:00] 407677463548919828: Hope that helps.

[2023-10-16 15:55:37] 204320873719660544: fwiw, out of the 2 clips you get from each chirp, check the last 10sec – this is the part that will be sampled to inform the next Continue chirp....

If the clip has 'ringing' or 'sampling gristle' or has too much reverb..., it's going to get progressively worse, and almost no way to clear the audio of that noise.

Ideally you want a good sample of the voice in that last 10sec – if there is no vocal there, the Continue will make up a new voice in the next chirp.

If the quality of that last 10sec is not good enough, consider regenerating that chirp.

[2023-10-17 16:25:54] 636706883859906562: the two protected components of audio:

> Melody - The order and rhythm of pitches that make up the main melody line of a piece of music is considered the unique work of the composer, it is protected. This can extend in part to the distinct melodic lines that also make up the harmonies of a song, referred to as Voice Leading. 
> 
> Lyrics - The collection of words in a song, whether spoken or sung, are also considered the unique work of the lyricist and are protected.

[2023-10-23 22:14:22] 944390296228220989: hey guys, im running the following code perfectly:

```python
GEN_TEMP = 0.6
SPEAKER = "v2/pt_speaker_0"
silence = np.zeros(int(0.08 * SAMPLE_RATE))  # quarter second of silence

pieces = []
for sentence in sentences:
    semantic_tokens = generate_text_semantic(
        sentence,
        history_prompt=SPEAKER,
        temp=GEN_TEMP,
        min_eos_p=0.05,  # this controls how likely the generation is to end
    )

    audio_array = semantic_to_waveform(semantic_tokens, history_prompt=SPEAKER,)
    pieces += [audio_array, silence.copy()]

```

[2023-10-24 14:40:37] 407677463548919828: I don't know who needs to hear this but for those who don't know...

There are some nice free tools out there to use for editing audio you produce with Suno Chirp.

There's vocalremover.org (which is free but has some limits to ho wmuch can be used in a time range)

This also exists to be run on your own local hardware: https://github.com/Anjok07/ultimatevocalremovergui

A free application which uses a lot of plugins on multiple platforms is Tenacity (forked from the Audacity application you may have heard of before): https://tenacityaudio.org/

There are others which I have not heard about, I'm sure.  But if *you* have never heard about these, now you know.  😉

[2023-10-24 20:16:43] 347175013142757390: You agree that the hallucinating is more relatable to the npz quality?
[2023-10-24 20:19:34] 614946962139250711: It's related in two ways. 1.) Some voices, especially cloned voices, might be unstable and hallucinate generally. 2.) If the language in the text prompt is very different than the language in the voice (Chinese/English, but even English-Slang/English-Fancy-Victorian-Novel. Oh and 3.) If the text prompt is the same as the text prompt 'inside' the voice, it hallucinates. So if you make a new voice, then use voice to speak exact like that created voice. (Edge case but worth mentioning.)
[2023-10-24 20:22:50] 347175013142757390: thank you
[2023-10-24 20:23:25] 614946962139250711: Actually just to cover the rest: 4.) Way too long text prompt. Just try packing the text prompt as full as you can, almost always hallucinates. Once in awhile it just reads beginning. 5.) Too short prompt (less than 5 words) make it somewhat more likely. 6.) Uses of [tags] can increase chances. Okay I'm out till tonight probably back latr
[2023-10-24 20:24:05] 347175013142757390: there's a thing nice in the rsxdalv ui, the semantic voice, many times i use it to make a walking stick for the audio voice

[2023-10-24 23:43:22] 347175013142757390: It's related in two ways. 1.) Some voices, especially cloned voices, might be unstable and hallucinate generally. 2.) If the language in the text prompt is very different than the language in the voice (Chinese/English, but even English-Slang/English-Fancy-Victorian-Novel. Oh and 3.) If the text prompt is the same as the text prompt 'inside' the voice, it hallucinates. So if you make a new voice, then use voice to speak exact like that created voice. (Edge case but worth mentioning.)

Actually just to cover the rest: 4.) Way too long text prompt. Just try packing the text prompt as full as you can, almost always hallucinates. Once in awhile it just reads beginning. 5.) Too short prompt (less than 5 words) make it somewhat more likely. 6.) Uses of [tags] can increase chances.
[2023-10-24 23:43:38] 347175013142757390: this is about hallucinating
[2023-10-24 23:43:49] 347175013142757390: I will organize this later as a list
[2023-10-24 23:43:54] 278614249234890752: i change the prompt a lot to check if it is consistant. but these parameters aren't helping me lol
[2023-10-24 23:44:14] 347175013142757390: maybe you should change the models of your UI

[2023-10-29 13:05:48] 234089364374683659: Also How do you end a song?
[2023-10-29 13:10:38] 407677463548919828: When you're done, you can try a couple of things.

`[outro]`  ⬅️  signifies to the AI you're looking for some music to play out towards an end.

`[fade out]
[fade out]
[fade out]
[fade out]
[fade out]` ⬅️ tells the AI to slowly fade the music out

I personally like to combine them when I can for better results.
[2023-10-29 13:11:42] 407677463548919828: Also, when you're happy with the ending, you can just hit the ❤️ on the segment that you'd prefer to be the ending part and that will stitch the previous continuations together to make one song of whatever length you had created with all your parts.

I'm trying yo generate long audios with BARK. But I think something is wrong with my code.

```
from bark import SAMPLE_RATE, generate_audio, preload_models
from scipy.io.wavfile import write as write_wav

def generate_voice_based_on_text(text: str, voice_type: str, base_dir: str) -> AudioSegment:
    uuid_str = str(uuid.uuid4())
    voice_type_bark = "[MAN]"
    if voice_type == "MULHER":
        voice_type_bark = "[WOMAN]"
    final_text = "{} {}".format(voice_type_bark, text)
    audio_array = generate_audio(final_text)
    write_wav("{}/tmp/{}.wav".format(base_dir, uuid_str), SAMPLE_RATE, audio_array)
    AudioSegment.from_wav("{}/tmp/{}.wav".format(base_dir, uuid_str))
```


I saw BARK that is limitated for 13-14 seconds.
Existe some way to remove this limitation?
